Free Talk

A Word of Insight·Long

Sunday, a day for indulging and rampant vices for Chinese people, rarely has any meaning of rest.

People only know the good of "having a son makes everything complete," but rarely know the freedom of being debt-free.

Living on loans is no better than drinking poison to quench thirst, because the interest generates more interest, inevitably leading to greater debt and no hope of repayment.

In the past, people read to understand principles, so there were sages in every generation. Nowadays, people study to become officials, leading to a decline in morality.

If our country's officials and merchants could turn their methods of deceiving compatriots to dealing with foreigners, the country's strength might have some hope of revival.

The psychology of fashionable women is like the unpredictable weather of the plum rain season.

To know if the war news reported in the newspaper is accurate, one must wait until the internal conflicts are resolved. So, during this period, it's better to read Free Talk to relieve boredom.

Misses wear high-heeled shoes to elevate their status and because they are troubled by their short height, trying to compete with mesdames in height.

If everyone wants to find someone more talented and beautiful than themselves as a companion, it will be in vain even with a lantern, because even if you find someone better than you, they will also turn a blind eye to you because they are looking for someone better than them.

Glimpses of the Chinese Exhibition and Fair During the Belgian Independence Anniversary

Hu Danqing, from Liege, Belgium

China's participation in the Belgian Centennial Independence Exhibition officially opened on the 16th of this month in Liege, Belgium. The exhibition is beautifully arranged, with vermilion columns and yellow palace lanterns all around. The exhibits are divided into five sections: one section for the Siku Beiyao (Complete Library in Four Sections) and writing tools and books, one section for embroidery and silk, one section for cloisonné and jade porcelain, and one section for silkworm cocoons and plant specimens. The central hall features a portrait of the Premier and the party and national flags. The hall is furnished with rosewood furniture, and the walls are decorated with embroidery. The area occupied by our exhibition is small, but it is dazzling, beautiful, and captivating, drawing praise from all who see it.

That evening, Chu Minyi hosted a banquet for the representatives of various delegations and Belgian celebrities. After the banquet, a fair was held at the Jardin d’Acclimation. The program included a flag presentation and the singing of the national anthem, clear singing of "The Civet Cat Prince for a Baby" by Ms. He Liangnan and Mr. Liu Xiutong, tai chi ball and tai chi stick performance by Chu Minyi, "Three Variations on the Plum Blossom" by Shen Chenglin, Chen Zhaoyu, Jin Yuzhang, and Zhuang Zhengbang, "Dumu Pass" by Chu Minyi, piano performance by Hu Shengfu, "Daiyu Burying Flowers" by Ms. Yang and Ms. Ma, "Daiyu Burying Flowers" by Ms. Xu Shiqi and Ms. Tong Xiuman, Jian Tzi performance by Shen Chenglin and Wu Peilang, "Sparrow and Child" by Ms. Qian Xiuling and Ms. Zhang Yuzhen, French song by Mr. Zhao Meibo, tai chi chuan and sword dance by Chu Minyi and Mr. Jin Shoufeng. Due to other engagement, Ms. Ma and Yang were unable to come to Liege. The committee telegrammed Yuan Xingjie and Yuan Xingci, two sisters from Paris who were traveling in Beijing, to sing Kunqu opera. Before each performance, Dr. Tian Enpei provided explanations and introductions, adding to the audience's interest. About forty or fifty Chinese students participated in the event, assigned by Chu to serve as temporary hosts or performers, all well-organized and spirited. This fair can be said to be China's first artistic contribution abroad. Although prepared in a short time, the results were very successful and not easy to achieve. I am writing this down to share with my compatriots.

Appreciating Snuff Bottles (Jun Mei)

Snuff was once popular a decade or so ago, with nobles and dignitaries all having a bottle in hand, but now it has gradually faded away. Our country's refined scholars are always fond of collecting things, such as paintings, calligraphy, antiques, and other objects. Even if they are incomplete or flawed, they are willing to acquire them at great expense. My cousin, Danlu, enjoys collecting snuff bottles, and over the years he has searched extensively and spent a lot of money, accumulating no less than one hundred different types of bottles. Some are shaped like teapots, some like wine cups, some like today's light bulbs, and some like ancient tripods and vessels. Some are as small as ink boxes, some as large as brush holders, some as flat as silver dollars, and some as long as bamboo tubes. The gourd shape is the most common, followed by the oval shape. Yesterday I went to visit him, and he graciously showed me several types, describing them in detail as if they were his own family treasures. Therefore, I am writing this down.

The jadeite bottle is shaped like a teacup, with a wide mouth and a small bottom, and a handle for carrying. It is carved from jadeite, and the carved flowers and birds are delicate and lifelike. The color is lustrous and flawless, with no nail marks on the bottom. There is a small seal on the bottom with four seal characters, which I could only identify after close examination as "Respectfully Presented by Tong He". My cousin said that this bottle was obtained by my late father from a eunuch when he was touring Beijing as an official. At that time, it was exchanged for one hundred silver dollars. When the Empress Dowager Cixi was in power, she was very fond of snuff, so the princes and dignitaries presented her with extraordinary gifts. The Empress Dowager was particularly fond of this bottle. During the Boxer Rebellion, when she fled in panic, the treasures in the palace were lost and stolen beyond counting. This bottle was also obtained at that time.

The purple stone bottle is shaped like a gourd, with a color like purple clay. The exterior is covered with white and green flowers, which are brilliant and dazzling. The slightly convex parts are decorated with delicate patterns. The bottom is purplish-blue. When illuminated in sunlight, the bottle reveals hidden erotic images of the Tang Palace. My cousin said that this bottle once belonged to Mr. Wei in Shanghai, but was later stolen by his servant and eventually came into my hands. The beauty of this bottle lies in the rarity of its stone. The figures that faintly appear in the bottle are actually painted on the inside. Only a local craftsman in Nanchang, Jiangxi, could do this, and the technique has now almost been lost. Therefore, this bottle is particularly precious.

A Record of the World's Heaviest Woman, Zoli (Huang Yingdai)

The arrival of Zoli, the world's heaviest woman, in Shanghai has caused quite a stir. Here are the details based on Western newspaper reports:

Ms. Zoli is an American, and her body weight is measured at 520 pounds, which is approximately 390-odd catties in Chinese weight. She is the heaviest woman in the world. She came to Shanghai last Tuesday aboard the Empress of Canada steamship, with the intention of touring the Far East. It is said that when she returns to her country, she will have to land in Shanghai for a second time. It is reported that Ms. Zoli is not only the heaviest woman in the world, but also that the weight of her entire family of seven is double that of ordinary people, totaling 3,137 pounds, with an average weight of 450 pounds per person. Her brother even weighs 721 pounds.

Ms. Zoli is only twenty-one years old this year. When she was born, she already weighed eighteen pounds. At the age of six, she reached 120 pounds, at twelve, 245 pounds, at eighteen, 457 pounds, and currently, she weighs 520 pounds. Looking at the records over the years, there is still the possibility of further development. Such obesity is truly unique and rare.

Given Zoli's great weight, when she walks, she moves with ease and without any difficulty. She has a good appetite on weekdays, and her health is unprecedented. She is also good at dancing, and she enjoys participating in various recreational activities and gatherings with a competitive nature. Long journeys are often difficult for her, but on this trip, Zoli came up with all sorts of interesting games to amuse herself and her fellow passengers. Her natural intelligence and witty remarks often caused people to burst into laughter. Having such a heavy woman on the journey greatly reduced travel weariness.

An Examination of Toads (Xiu Jun)

Toads are smaller than frogs and also belong to the frog family. I read an account of a large toad, weighing five catties, described by the Qing Scholar, which I found astonishing. I suspect the golden-backed toad described in *Youyang Zazu* wasn't this large either. After further research, I found that these creatures can indeed be as large as a plate, a cauldron, or a bed. Weighing five catties is not that large. A description follows:

The *Old Book of Tang, Treatise on the Five Elements*, states: "During the Shenlong era, there was a toad in the Wei River as big as a stone cauldron. The people of the village gathered to watch for several days, and then it disappeared. That year, there was a great flood that swept away hundreds of families in the capital." The *Tang Book, Treatise on the Five Elements*, states: "In the second year of Xiantian, in the sixth month, a large snake, more than ten feet long, emerged from under the bricks of the court hall in the capital. There was also a large toad as big as a plate with eyes as red as fire, fighting each other. Suddenly, the snake entered a large tree, and the toad entered the grass." Furthermore, the *Old Book of Tang, Treatise on the Five Elements*, states: "A month before Li Kui became Chancellor, a large toad as big as a bed was seen in his room and then suddenly disappeared. The diviner interpreted this as the Toad Celestial, indicating an event of good fortune."

In conclusion, from the above, aside from the one entering the grass, one suddenly disappeared, and the other disappeared after several days. Could it be that toads can also transform unpredictably? If so, how can we explain the large toad weighing five catties caught by a villager in a certain village in Loudong?

Based on what we have researched, there is also one extremely strange event that has never happened before: a toad making sounds inside a pillar. A supplementary account follows: In the Ningzhen Temple in Huaizhou, during the Tang Dynasty, the eastern corridor pillar had been there for over fifty years. The Taoist priests often heard the sound of a toad inside the pillar but did not know its exact location. Later, because the pillar was rotten, it was replaced. The cook chopped it up for firewood and found a toad inside the pillar. The pillar had no holes beforehand, according to the *Records of the Five Elements*. How could the toad have entered the pillar without a hole in the corridor pillar? Even if the pillar had been there for fifty years, the Taoist priests heard the toad sound when the pillar was intact as before. If it had not been replaced because the pillar was rotten, or if the cook had not chopped it up for firewood, how would anyone have known there was a toad inside the pillar? This matter is even more extraordinary than the large toad weighing five catties. It shows how vast the universe is, and there is no end to wonders. This is also a matter that cannot be fully understood.

Impressions of a Trip to the East (4) (Qian Hua)

Giant Cauldron at Chongfu Temple

The reporter and Mr. Huang disembarked and began their tour. As soon as they left the pier, they were surrounded by dozens of rickshaws, each vying for their attention. They respectfully offered their services, claiming to take responsibility for guiding the tour of the entire city for only one and a half yen per day. Their words were sincere, and there was no sign of the exorbitant demands often made of foreign visitors. Finally, they settled on a price of one yen and twenty sen per rickshaw. Their first destination was Zepfang Park, supposedly Nagasaki's only scenic spot. The road wound up and down, and the rickshaw moved very slowly, as slow as walking. As the saying goes, "walking is as good as riding," but in this case, "riding is as good as walking." After about ten minutes, they arrived at the park gate. The flowers were blooming in profusion, and the ancient trees towered overhead, creating a refreshing atmosphere. The rickshaw pullers led the way, and as they passed each point of interest, they explained and pointed, their words flowing incessantly, which made the experience even more engaging. Zepfang Park is named after Zepfang Mountain and covers a wide area with excellent facilities. There is a public library and a museum, showing the Japanese people's attention to public entertainment venues. At the top of the mountain is a tea room selling various drinks and food, decorated with delicate cleanliness and served by beautiful women, accompanied by the melodious sounds of radio. Sitting in the room, one cannot help but be captivated. Looking down from the window, the entire panorama of Nagasaki is clearly visible. Further ahead from the tea room is the Zepfang Shrine, which is like a Chinese temple. The architecture is also similar. In front of the stone steps of the main hall, the guide, the rickshaw puller, stood upright, clapped his hands, and closed his eyes in silence for about a minute, saying that it was the Japanese way of showing respect to the gods, like kneeling and bowing in our country. Leaving the shrine gate, they descended the steps directly to the park gate and then boarded the rickshaw again to visit the Chinese Chongfu Temple. Chongfu Temple is located on Mount Shousheng, about a li from Zepfang Park. It is a Zen monastery founded by pure Chinese. In recent years, the presiding monk passed away and was replaced by the Japanese. The reporter, due to the limited time, did not have time to investigate its origins, otherwise, it would have been an extremely interesting historical material. The architecture of the temple also imitates the Han style, quite grand. The plaques and couplets are all in Chinese, such as "The Dharma is vast," and so on. Above the main gate, the four characters "Chongfu Zen Temple" are written in bold, with elegant calligraphy, undoubtedly the work of a famous writer. There are no monks in the temple, and it is managed by a certain Japanese person. Upon entering, it was completely silent, but everything was still intact. In the main hall, various Buddha statues are sculpted, but the gold leaf has peeled off, and inches of dirt have accumulated, indicating the desolate state of incense. In the left corner of the hall is a huge iron cauldron, surrounded by a rice fence. The top of the fence is covered with Japanese paper strips, almost entirely, looking like talismans. On the cauldron, it is written in green ink: "The Giant Cauldron for Porridge Donation at Mount Shousheng Chongfu Zen Temple, Made in the Renxu Year, Second Month of the Tianhe Era." According to the rickshaw puller, about three hundred years ago, Nagasaki suffered a great famine, and people in the city ate each other. A certain Elder of Chongfu Temple was greatly compassionate and urgently sent his disciples to use Buddhist Dharma to transport a hundred dan of white rice from China, along with this giant cauldron, to cook porridge in the temple and provide relief, saving the lives of hundreds of villagers, who were grateful for it. The villagers specially preserved this cauldron as a memorial, and it is said that China and Japan have always been like lips and teeth. Speaking of Nagasaki, the relationship is especially close. Although the rickshaw puller's words are mythological, they are not without foundation. The giant cauldron was transported from China, but at that time, there was definitely no such thing. It must have been cast locally, but it is also commendable. It was already four o'clock in the afternoon, and they dared not linger any longer, hurriedly ordering a return.

Correspondence from the East (10) (1) (Wu Xiaohou)

(4) Hygienic Testing Laboratory The Hygienic Testing Laboratory is also an important facility in health administration. Currently, it is responsible for specialized investigations and research on various aspects of hygiene in Tokyo City, as well as microscopic, microbiological, medical-chemical, physical, and hygienic examinations, the issuance of certificates for pharmaceutical products, physical examinations, health clinics, preventive vaccinations, and the promotion and dissemination of hygienic knowledge and the preparation of preventive medicines for infectious diseases. According to statistics, the total number of tests conducted throughout the year in Showa 3 was 5,853 for Tokyo City's water quality testing, 2,699 for sewage and other special tests, 6,294 for tests commissioned by various related bureaus and departments of the city, and 11,047 for tests commissioned by other general citizens, totaling 25,893 tests. The main projects undertaken by the laboratory are roughly divided into four categories: (1) hygiene consultation, (2) hygiene education, (3) pharmaceutical preparation, and (4) commissioned testing.

(5) Overview of Commerce, Industry, and Encouragement of Industry in Tokyo City Although Tokyo City is a political district and not an industrial area like Osaka, Yokohama, or Kobe, the development of its production in recent years has made it one of the industrial hubs of Japan. Therefore, an independent Commerce and Industry Section is established directly under the Second Assistant to the Mayor. The prominent commercial and industrial facilities are two:

(1) Commercial and industrial facilities are roughly divided into three types: (1) Encouragement of industry, divided into five categories: (1) Expositions and fairs, with 22 locations, and the city's subsidy amount is more than 84,000 yen. (2) Commercial and industrial consultations, namely commercial and industrial visits, introductions, and mediation activities. (3) Industrial organizations, namely trade associations, with 91 groups and 67,671 members, and 163 quasi-associations with 36,593 members. (4) Industrial surveys, namely surveys of businesses and factories, important industrial products and special products, freight collection and distribution, and ship traffic, as well as the actual situation of small and medium-sized businesses. (5) Industrial friendly gatherings, namely gatherings of the entire city's industrial community for friendly conversations to exchange opinions and refine and improve all facilities. (2) Finance, divided into six categories: (1) Credit unions, (2) financing and repayment methods, (3) construction assistance, (4) financing of working capital for small and medium-sized businesses, (5) payment of subsidies, and (6) surveys of popular finance. (3) Weights and measures control: In Showa 4, the Ministry of Commerce and Industry (like our country's Ministry of Industry and Commerce) stipulated a nationwide unified system of weights and measures. The Commerce and Industry Section follows the stipulated laws and regulations to carry out unified control throughout the city.

(2) Market facilities: Tokyo has five municipal vegetable markets: (1) Sanweixian Small Retail Market, (2) Central Wholesale Market, (3) Tsukiji Fish Market, Kanda Produce Market, and (5) Koto Produce Market. In addition, for the sake of meat hygiene and economic relations in the city, a slaughterhouse is also set up. On this day, the reporter visited each market and returned to the Jihua Society. There, he received a letter of introduction from Yunnan Provincial Committee member Zhang Chunou to the Tokyo Municipal Investigation Committee, sent by Huang Jingwan from Shanghai. Also, Jiang Bohan, the supervisor of students studying in Japan, and the Fujianese students Lin Zongxi and Qiu Bizhen and his wife visited one after another and enjoyed chatting. After the visitors left, the barking of dogs and the night wind and rain filled the window, preventing sleep. Dressed, he got up to play dominoes and wrote three poems to send home, saying: "Thousands of mountains and rivers, each in our own corner of the earth. I frequently tell the dominoes, longing with an eager eye. Every day I dream of you, do you dream of me? The wanderer is as thin as a yellow flower under the sea and sky." Also: "Traveling East again, guest poems sent. I count the days of return, not yet fixed. The wind and rain are merciless, adding to my hatred. What is most difficult to dispel is the sorrow of separation." Also: "How many times have I lingered under the green banana window? On the fifteenth of the month, I remember old times." (My wife sent a poem with the line "I still remember the moonlit night last winter.") The sound of dogs barking prevents sleep. I light a lamp and remotely recall the ancient stone heads.

The Gold Market's Movement Is Erratic

The changes in the morning and afternoon markets... were in inverse proportion.

Floating and unsteady, as if languid. Yesterday, the attitude toward standard gold was floating and inconsistent. The morning market appeared strong despite weakness, with fluctuations of nine taels. The afternoon market turned from strong to weak, with advances and delays of six taels. The situation was chaotic and unpredictable, ultimately resulting in a decline. The foreign exchange market was starkly different, with the posted rate increasing by half a point. Internally, because the banks' appetite was not bad, they were still able to stand firm. Buying and selling among dealers was very tight, with buyers seeming to be active. Zhifeng Yong, Wanxing, Fuchang, and Yongfeng all bought in, while Dadecheng, Yuanmao Yong, Chunyuan Yong, etc., all sold. Since the silver market continued to rise in the morning, it opened very weakly and broke the 590 tael barrier. Ministry of Finance

Encouraging Export Goods

Regardless of Whether They Are Locally Made, Machine-Made, or Imitation

Only Collect Export Tax Once

Yesterday, the Jianghai Customs Superintendent Office received an instruction from the Ministry of Finance, which read: "In order to address the issue of the decline in exports due to the preciousness of gold and the cheapness of silver domestically, this Ministry has decided to encourage the export of goods. All merchants who transport and sell overseas products, regardless of whether they are locally made, machine-made, or imitation, shall only pay export tax once at the nearest customs office. After passing through various customs offices, they will only be inspected against the list and will no longer pay tax. Please comply with this instruction and inform your subordinates to comply as well." Furthermore, it is learned that the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance has also received the above-mentioned order to instruct its subordinate donation bureaus that they shall not cause difficulties for locally made and imitation goods that have already paid export tax, and should promptly verify and release them to show encouragement.

Foreign Company Registration

The Executive Yuan Announces Measures

The Principle of Reciprocity is Adopted

Since the case of the Japanese Mitsui & Co. was filed, the problem of foreign companies registering as legal entities was raised by Chinese lawyers, and it was once noticed by the legal and various circles. This matter was decided by the 334th meeting of the National Government, and the Legislative Yuan and the Executive Yuan were ordered to revise and promulgate it. The following is an excerpt from the letter from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to the Shanghai Merchant Association: "The members of the Shanghai Merchant Association are hereby informed that foreign companies setting up companies in China, whether head offices or branches, shall apply for registration in accordance with Chinese laws and regulations in order to obtain the status of a legal person. However, it has been found that the policies adopted by various countries for the registration of foreign companies are different. Some treat foreign companies the same as companies established by their own citizens, while others adopt the principle of mutual recognition, with the prerequisite that the other country allows companies of their own country to register in their country. Still others, in addition to mutual recognition, set various other restrictions. In view of China's current situation, being too lenient with the registration of companies from various countries would easily lead to abuse, which is not acceptable. However, too strict restrictions would in fact be difficult to implement. It seems appropriate to adopt a compromise approach. It is proposed to adopt the principle of mutual recognition, and the approval or rejection of a company's registration should be conditional on whether the other country allows companies of our country to register in their country. A slight restriction should be added to equal treatment. After detailed discussion by the National Government, it has been decided that the registration of foreign companies should be based on the principle of reciprocity, with the prerequisite that the other country allows companies of our country of the same type to register in their country, except where there are legal restrictions. Accordingly, this letter is recorded and communicated to the merchants of the city to avoid many disputes. Sincerely, Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Industry and Commerce."

Shanghai-Hankou Air Mail Can Be Delivered on the Same Day

Reasons for Changing the Time

According to the postal authorities, the timetable for airmail between Shanghai and Hankou has been changed since the 1st of this month as follows:

Upstream: Leaves Shanghai at 8:00 am, arrives in Nanjing at 10:15 am, leaves Nanjing at 10:30 am, arrives in Jiujiang at 1:15 pm, leaves Jiujiang at 1:30 pm, arrives in Hankou at 3:00 pm.

Downstream: Leaves Hankou at 8:00 am, arrives in Jiujiang at 9:30 am, leaves Jiujiang at 9:45 am, arrives in Nanjing at 12:30 pm, leaves Nanjing at 11:45 am, arrives in Shanghai at 3:00 pm.

The time for sealing and sending airmail at the Shanghai Bureau has not changed. However, since this change in flight schedule, airmail from Hankou can be delivered on the afternoon of the day it arrives in Shanghai.

Central Explanation of the Law on the Organization of Industrial and Commercial Associations

Not Restricted by the Organizational Procedures of People's Organizations

The organization of industrial and commercial associations in this city has always followed the organizational procedures of people's organizations stipulated by the Second Plenary Session, which requires the endorsement of more than 50 initiators with residences in the local area and the permission of the party headquarters before applying for registration. Since the promulgation of the Law on Industrial and Commercial Guilds, Article 3 of which states that the establishment of an industrial and commercial guild requires the initiation of more than seven companies and firms before applying for establishment, the Municipal Social Bureau, in view of the obvious conflict between the two laws and regulations, specifically presented to the Municipal Government and forwarded it to the Executive Yuan for explanation. It is heard that the Municipal Government received instructions from the Executive Yuan to separately transfer the matter to the Legislative Yuan and the Central Executive Committee for verification and instruction, as it involved legal and party affairs. Subsequently, the Commercial Law Drafting Committee checked and verified the explanation of the Training Department, stating that the organization of chambers of commerce and industrial and commercial guilds is based on the premise of public guilds and shops as units, and companies and firms as units, which is different from other types of people's organizations that are based on individuals as organizational units. The initiators of the organization can be exempted from the restrictions of the organizational plan of people's organizations and should still be handled in accordance with the regulations of the respective laws. Moreover, in accordance with legislative practice, the application of special laws takes precedence over ordinary laws and can be followed accordingly. The Municipal Government has ordered the Social Bureau to forward the notification to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for separate notification.

Wireless Radio Receiver

Registration Required Within One Month

Failure to Comply Will Be Considered Private Installation

The Wireless Radio General Administration of the Ministry of Communications of this port, having received an order from the ministry to prepare for the establishment of a wireless radio broadcasting station, is now actively proceeding with it. Those in various places who have installed their own wireless radio receivers must first register. The provisional measures have been drafted by the administration and submitted to the ministry for approval, and will be implemented immediately. The Provisional Measures for the Registration of Wireless Radio Receivers are recorded below: Article 1: Anyone who installs a wireless radio receiver for the purpose of listening to wireless news, speeches, business information, music, etc. shall request registration in accordance with the provisions of these provisional measures. Article 2: Anyone who wishes to install a wireless radio receiver, whether purchased or assembled from parts, shall register with the Wireless Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications or the registration office designated by the Wireless Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications, fill out an application form for registration of a wireless radio receiver, and obtain a registration certificate before being allowed to use it. This registration procedure is temporarily free of charge. Article 3: Wireless radio receivers purchased or assembled from parts must meet the following two requirements: (1) The internal devices cannot be arbitrarily changed for transmitting or speaking purposes. (2) Must not generate strong oscillations. Article 4: After the installing household obtains the registration certificate, if the registration office designated by the Wireless Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications considers that there are any questions, it may order it to submit the machinery for inspection or send personnel to inspect it, and must not obstruct it. Article 5: When the address of the installing household changes or the machine procedure changes, the location of the old and new installation sites or the old and new machine procedure shall be stated, together with the previously obtained registration certificate, to the Wireless Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications or the registration office designated by the Wireless Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications to apply for correction. All correction procedures are temporarily free of charge. Article 6: Wireless radio receiver registration certificates shall not be replaced or rented out. Article 7: Those who have registered with the Wireless Radio Administration Office of the Construction Committee and obtained a wireless radio receiver registration license shall continue to be valid, but shall be exchanged for the new registration certificate specified in the preceding paragraph. Article 8: The above-mentioned procedure for exchanging for a new registration certificate shall be limited to one month after the announcement of the approval of these provisional measures. If the deadline is exceeded, it shall be considered a private installation. Article 9: If the installing household receives any wireless radio message from its receiver other than broadcast radio, it shall keep it confidential. Article 10: The antenna used by the installing household shall not be close to telegraph, telephone, electric light or other power lines. The antenna entering the house shall be equipped with a lightning arrester, or in the event of a thunderstorm, the antenna shall be connected to the ground wire to prevent danger. Article 11: If the installing household wishes to stop listening to broadcast radio, it shall immediately dismantle the machine and antenna, and notify the Wireless Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications to cancel the registration and return the registration certificate. In the future, if it wishes to reinstall it for use or transfer it to others, it shall re-register in accordance with the new household regulations. Article 11: The machine program and wavelength range of the wireless radio receiver installed by the installing household will not be restricted temporarily. Article 13: Anyone who has not registered with the Wireless Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications and has not applied for a registration certificate and privately installs a wireless radio receiver shall, once discovered, in addition to confiscating the entire machine, be fined from 10 yuan to 100 yuan depending on the circumstances. Article 14: These provisional measures shall be repealed after the promulgation of the official regulations for wireless radio receivers. Article 15: If there are any matters not covered in these provisional measures, they shall be submitted for amendment at any time. Article 16: These provisional measures shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Ministry of Communications.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce States the Evils of Parcel Post Tax

A Telegram Is Sent Requesting Submission to the Tax Reduction Committee for Abolition

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, saying: "We have checked the file and received a joint announcement from the Postal Workers' Union and the Postal Staff Union stating that the parcel post tax is something that did not exist in the past. During the era of warlord separatism, some provinces used the excuse that parcel post did not pay the likin tax and created this type of tax in order to collect money and expand their military. However, there was no complete organization. After our National Government established its capital in Nanjing, the Ministry of Finance followed the old examples and reorganized and expanded it, establishing special offices to supervise the matter. General bureaus were set up in each province, and branch offices were established in counties and cities. The system of parcel post tax was thus established. However, since its establishment, more than two years have passed, and the resulting malpractices have been unbearable. We would like to briefly state them for your review: Parcel post parcels sent to commercial ports must pass through customs for inspection and payment of regular taxes and sundry taxes such as child tariff, wharf, and Qingpu taxes, which are already quite substantial. Then, the Parcel Post Tax Bureau adds a 2.5% tax, and when the parcel arrives in the interior, the local Parcel Post Tax Bureau levies another 2.5% tax. In this way, one item is taxed multiple times, and each tax is levied. The suffering of the merchants is self-evident. The inconvenience of the cumbersome procedures of repeated inspections by customs and tax bureaus when sending parcels is another matter. According to an article in the May issue of the British Chamber of Commerce Magazine, we would like to translate it to provide proof. The original text says: 'Finance Minister Song said that the parcel post tax is not a new tax, but a type of likin tax. However, the likin tax does not apply to parcels coming from abroad, nor does it apply to parcels going to Chinese commercial ports, nor does it apply to parcels going to the interior and passing through a commercial port. Now, all are taxed. The only parcels not taxed are those sent from abroad to China. Furthermore, this parcel post tax does not follow the customs valuation method, so it is always higher than the customs tax rate. The likin tax only collects its due, while the parcel post tax collects both the origin and destination. For example, if there is silk weighing one hundred pounds sent from Shanghai to Beijing, the tax payment comparison is as follows: (1) Sent by parcel post: postage 6.6 yuan, customs tax 41.4 yuan, parcel post tax 9 yuan, totaling 57 yuan; (2) Sent by railway passenger car: freight 3.94 yuan, likin tax 17 yuan, totaling 20.94 yuan; (3) Sent by railway freight car: freight 0.22 yuan, likin tax 17 yuan, totaling 17.32 yuan. If such a bad method is not abolished, the fastest and most reliable postal transportation in the country will disappear from now on.' Currently, many parcels are abandoned by the post office and sent through other channels because other transportation agencies charge much lower taxes for carrying the same type of goods via the same route, and the procedures are also simpler. As a result, the number of parcels received by the post office has gradually decreased. Taking Shanghai as an example, before the establishment of the Parcel Post Tax Bureau, the number of parcels received by the post office increased year by year. After the establishment of the bureau, the result was the opposite. In the 16th year of the Republic of China, the post office received 1,013,240 parcels, while in March, April, and May of this year, it only received 192,079 parcels. Parcel post has always been the main source of income for the post office, but the obstruction of the parcel post tax has caused the economy to be cut in half and expenses are not covered. The post office is a profit-making enterprise for the country, and the Parcel Post Tax Bureau is a tax revenue agency for the country. They are both under the jurisdiction of the government, so why should they be divided? It is only because it is beneficial to finance that they forget the harm to transportation. It is like cutting flesh to mend a sore on the arm. It is a mistake of the wise. From this, it can be seen that the parcel post tax is indeed harmful to merchants and people and severely burdens the post office. It was originally intended to compensate for the likin tax, but it is nothing more than a disguised form of likin tax. The central government has already declared that it will abolish the likin tax from October 10th of this year, and the Ministry of Finance also plans to convene a meeting on the abolition of the likin tax on the 10th of this month. Therefore, this disguised form of likin tax, the parcel post tax, should be abolished uniformly in order to completely abolish the bad tax system and abolish redundant agencies at the same time. The matter concerns both tax and postal administration and cannot be ignored. We must unanimously urge the government department to include the parcel post tax in the agenda of the tax reduction meeting and resolve to abolish it in order to alleviate the post office's difficulties and alleviate the merchants' suffering." The chamber considered this matter a commercial hardship and sent letters to relevant industry groups to solicit opinions on the abolition of the parcel post tax, detailing the meetings and forwarding the cases. According to a reply from the Shanghai Silk Industry Group Consolidation Committee, the case was submitted to the fourth Consolidation Committee for discussion. It was unanimously agreed that this parcel post tax is indeed a kind of disguised likin tax that harms merchants and people, and the silk industry suffers the most. The telegrams from the Postal Workers' Union have already explained it in detail. The former Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Silk Industry Branch, the China National Silk Shanghai Relief Association, and the Silk, Cigarette, Match, and Soap Industry Federation have all previously submitted cases to the government authorities requesting abolition. Now that the Ministry of Finance's tax reduction meeting has opened, your chamber should submit it to the Central Party Department, the National Government, and the Executive Yuan, ordering the tax reduction committee to include this parcel post onerous tax on the agenda and resolve to abolish it in order to alleviate the suffering of the silk industry. In view of this, the chamber believes that the parcel post tax is a disguised likin tax that has been publicly recognized by all sectors. Since its establishment and collection, there have been many malpractices and it has been criticized by all merchants. According to the British Chamber of Commerce Magazine, for example, the cost of transporting silk weighing one hundred pounds from Shanghai to Beijing by post is more than twice as high as by road. The disadvantages have long been understood by your Excellency. Moreover, since the parcel post tax became popular, the post office's parcel income has sharply decreased. Both are national tax revenue agencies, but this surplus and that deficit have little increase in tax revenue. At this time when tax reduction is about to be implemented, the Postal Workers' Union and the Silk Industry Group's application for the abolition of the proposal is indeed the only requirement to improve the tax law and eliminate commercial difficulties. In view of the above-mentioned circumstances, we should telegraph your ministry to review and approve the proposal to resolutely abolish it in order to avoid onerous taxes and demonstrate the restoration of prosperity. This is a public convenience. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce bows respectfully.

Cultivating Talents for International Shipping Routes

Chen Tianjun, Section Chief of the Naval Department's Political Affairs Division, previously believed that in order to develop China's nascent shipping industry, it was necessary to train maritime talents as a prerequisite, and that practical training was an important subject for maritime studies. Since China has no ships operating on international routes, it is not easy to visit foreign countries. Therefore, last year, after taking office, Section Chief Chen sent letters to various foreign shipping companies requesting them to arrange for Chinese trainees on their ships. The British Company and the Likmao Company replied and agreed. Section Chief Chen has repeatedly contacted the Shanghai Shipping Association, Wusong Merchant Marine School, Fisheries School, and various groups to guarantee the trainees and send them to serve on ships. The fees are low and the results are effective, and the shipping companies are deeply in favor of it. Recently, Section Chief Chen received a letter from the German Henburg Company agreeing to send trainees on board for practical training and has sent letters to various groups related to the shipping industry to send trainees again.

New Information on Pacific Shipping

China and the United States Add New Ships: Within the Sino-American Pacific route this year, Britain, the United States, Japan, and Norway have all increased the number of new ships, competing with full spirit on speed. Generally, the horsepower of the new ships must travel at least 17 nautical miles per hour, and the battle between the mail ships is even fiercer, with some increasing to 19 knots and some increasing to 20 knots. The fast ship fever of the Atlantic shipping world has become prevalent on the Pacific route. The British Smith Shipping Company has never had Sino-American liners. This time, it has specially dispatched more than ten new-style cargo ships of 10,000 tons to Shanghai to open up a new Sino-American route. The route is from Shanghai to Houston in the United States and via Japan. Houston is a concentration point for silk going to the United States and an important port for the export of American cotton. Ships such as Seattle City, Wengu City, Victoria City, and Atlantic City have been dispatched to Shanghai. In the Far East, Xiangtai Foreign Firm has been entrusted with the management. From now on, there will be another British shipping company on the Sino-American route, together with the original Japanese, American, Norwegian, and British shipping companies, making a total of 19 companies operating. The total number of ships has exceeded 200.

The Price of Lake Silk Shipping Is Negotiated To Increase: After the recent silver drop and gold rise, the shipping prices of all routes have increased. Only the Lake Silk freight on the Sino-American route has not been able to increase since the price was reduced due to the disturbance of the Japanese shipping companies. This is because most of the shipping companies have contracts with the customers. However, the price from Shanghai to Hoboken, which was originally US$4 per 100 pounds, has now increased to US$4.20. The shipping companies also plan to slightly increase the freight from Shanghai to San Francisco and other places, which is US$1 per 100 pounds, otherwise the losses will be too great, and the meager US$1 is not enough to cover the cost of the wharf. It is currently being negotiated with the various companies.

Rikuju Maru Is Also Completed: The second new ship built by Nippon Yusen Kaisha on the Seattle route, the Rikuju Maru, is a sister ship to the Hikawamaru, which arrived in Shanghai yesterday. Both are fast ships of 11,000 tons. It has also been completed and is being equipped with passenger seats, scheduled to start the first voyage on August 23.

Crew of the Shipwrecked Dippodo Arrive in Shanghai

After the Norwegian ship Dippodo of the Kailuan Company was sunk by the Japanese ship Fengtian Maru in Shandong Bay, its crew members and sailors who fell into the sea have returned to Shanghai from Dalian on the Fengtian Maru. They arrived in Shanghai last night and landed at the Huangpu Wharf. Captain Johnson also came with them. Kailuan is now first inquiring about the truth of the accident and then planning the salvage and arbitration.

Two Leather Factories in Zhabei Call for Protection

The Tongliyuan and Chengfa leather factories on Zhangqiao Road in Zhabei sent a letter to the Guangzhou-Zhao Guild Hall, the Overseas Chinese Federation, and the Yueqiao Federation, saying: "Dear Sirs, we are writing to you. Our factories are located on Zhangqiao Road in Zhabei. The two factories are connected, but because the location is remote and extremely desolate, there has never been a guard post set up in the nearby miles to protect it, and there are no police patrols because it is far from the city. As a result, local hooligans and bandits often dismantle and steal from our factories. For example, on the night of May 1 and June 24 of this year, the fence of our Chengfa Leather Factory was pried open by these people, and they broke into the factory and stole a total of 13 pieces of cooked Hu green buffalo hide in two times. It has been reported to the third branch of the fifth district for investigation, and the stolen goods have not been recovered. The representative of the Lingnan Tongqun Litiyu Association also presented a request to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to strictly arrest the perpetrators. However, the ink was not dry and the case has not been closed. On June 28, at 6 pm, two bandits dismantled the Tongliyuan Leather Factory and tried to steal the buffalo hide. Manager Dai Ying came out to negotiate and was beaten. They then gathered hundreds of bandits to the Tongliyuan Leather Factory, smashed the door, and swarmed in, beating anyone they saw and destroying the leather-making equipment in the factory and robbing property. More than ten innocent factory workers were beaten. Such rampant behavior is truly fearless of the law. If no measures are taken to protect them, the consequences will be unbearable. Although the Public Security Bureau captured a few perpetrators at the time, there are still many fugitives who should be strictly arrested and brought to justice in order to curb the banditry. Our colleagues have been engaged in the buffalo hide business in Nanyang. Due to the bullying of foreigners, we have returned to China together to revitalize the industry and open leather factories to do our best to love the country. However, we have paid the merchants' obligations such as police fees and room donations. If the protection is not thorough, where can we enjoy the right to local peace? Therefore, our factories often suffer from hooligans and bandits dismantling and stealing. The pain of being beaten by these people on the afternoon of June 28 is that we want to close down the business, but the previous efforts are in vain and the capital is gone. If we continue to do business and the local hooligans and bandits destroy it, if we do not plan for a good aftermath, the suffering in the future will be worse than today. We are forced to ask your guild hall to ask the municipal government to transfer the municipal public security bureau to set up a real guard post near our factory and send more police patrols to protect it. Please send a letter to the local court to handle the case impartially and severely punish the criminals and hooligans involved in the case, and strictly arrest the remaining accomplices so that the bandits cannot escape justice and our factories can be at peace. Thank you. The Tongliyuan Leather Factory and Chengfa Leather Factory in Zhabei, Shanghai, sincerely submit."

Central Bank Inspection Report

The Fifty-Eighth Time

The Fifty-Ninth Inspection Report on the Central Bank's Issuance Reserves states that this association is responsible for inspecting the Bank's issuance of convertible note reserves in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations. The fifty-ninth inspection was held at the Bank's Issuance Bureau on July 10, 19th year of the Republic of China. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: The total amount of convertible notes issued is 16,757,043 silver dollars, including 15,664,822 silver dollar notes and 1,092,221 silver dollars in subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note reserves is 16,757,043 silver dollars, including 13,867,544.60 silver dollars in cash reserves. The cash reserves include 10,868,136.73 silver dollars stored in the Bank's Issuance Vault, 1,200,335.14 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 1,796,372.73 silver dollars stored in the same industry. The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 2,889,498.40 silver dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guaranteed reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. Provisional Regulations for the Management of Veterinarians

The Municipal Government announced yesterday:

The Municipal Government announced yesterday the "Provisional Regulations for the Management of Veterinarians in this City," stating: "Now, the Provisional Regulations for the Management of Veterinarians in Shanghai Municipality are hereby formulated and promulgated."

Provisional Regulations for the Management of Veterinarians in Shanghai Municipality Article 1: All veterinarians practicing within the city limits shall, before the Central Government promulgates the Veterinarian Law, uniformly comply with these Provisional Regulations. Article 2: Veterinarians who have not passed the examination or review according to the regulations shall not be registered; those who have not been registered shall not practice within the city limits. Article 3: The examination or review of veterinarians shall be conducted by the Bureau of Health, which shall hire several veterinarians of excellent character and learning and with rich experience to form a Veterinary Examination Committee. Article 4: Veterinary examinations shall be held once every June. Article 5: Veterinarians who do not possess the following qualifications for exemption from examination and registration shall apply for examination in accordance with the regulations and pay an examination fee of ten silver dollars at the time of application. Those who fail the first examination may pay half of the examination fee when applying for the next examination. Article 6: Veterinarians who have passed the examination or review shall pay a registration and license fee of six silver dollars and a stamp tax of one silver dollar per person. Article 7: Applicants for examination shall submit a letter of intent, resume, and two recent 4-inch half-length photographs, along with the examination fee, to the Bureau of Health before the start of the examination period in accordance with the prescribed format. Article 8: The examination shall be divided into written and oral examinations. Those who pass the written examination shall then take the oral examination. Those who pass the oral examination shall be allowed to register and be issued a license to practice. Article 9: The subjects of the examination are as follows: (1) Anatomy (2) Physiology (3) Histology (4) Pathology (5) Bacteriology (6) Pharmacology (7) Surgery (8) Internal Medicine (9) Chemistry (10) Infectious Diseases (11) Meat Inspection (12) Dairy Inspection Article 10: An average score of 70 or above in each subject shall be considered passing. Except for foreigners, written answers shall be in the national language. Foreigners may choose one of the following languages for the examination: English, French, Japanese, or German. The same applies to the oral examination. Article 11: Those who possess one of the following qualifications shall be granted exemption from examination, registration, and license to practice after review and approval, and shall be exempt from paying the examination fee: (A) Graduates of veterinary medicine or veterinary specialty schools of government-established, public, or registered private universities in the country who have obtained a certificate. (B) Graduates of veterinary medicine or veterinary specialty schools of government-established, public, or private universities abroad who have obtained a certificate. Article 12: If the Examination Committee encounters any doubts during the review, it may send a letter to the Bureau of Health for investigation or notify the person under review to submit supplementary evidence or order them to attend a meeting for questioning in order to determine whether to accept or reject them. Article 13: Veterinarians who possess exemption qualifications shall submit a letter of intent, resume, and two recent 4-inch half-length photographs, along with the graduation certificate and other certificates, to the Bureau of Health for review 15 days before the start of the examination period in accordance with the prescribed format. Article 14: Veterinarians who have passed the review shall be issued a veterinarian's practice license. Those who have passed the examination shall be issued a veterinarian's practice license. Article 15: Those who practice veterinary medicine within the city limits without registration and a license issued by the Bureau of Health shall be subject to a fine of up to 200 yuan and shall be ordered to cease operations. Article 16: Each veterinarian shall display the practice license issued by the Bureau in a conspicuous place for public viewing as proof. Article 17: The practice license obtained by each veterinarian shall be submitted for verification once every January. After verification, it shall be stamped and returned. Article 18: If a veterinarian loses their license, they shall immediately apply for a replacement. However, they shall pay the registration and license fee and stamp tax in accordance with the provisions of Article 6 and publish a statement in the newspaper declaring the old license invalid. Article 19: If a veterinarian's place of practice is relocated, they shall report it to the Bureau of Health for record within two weeks. Violators shall be subject to a fine of up to ten yuan. Article 20: These Provisional Regulations may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 21: These Provisional Regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Promulgation of Regulations for District Branches of the Citizens' Association

Submitted to the Municipal Party Department for approval after discussion by the Standing Committee.

The Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation has repeatedly discussed and formulated the organizational regulations for district branches at the plenary session of the committee. The district branch regulations were drafted, and Yu Hualong, Wang Yansong, Zhang Yichen, Yu Zhongxian, Wang Pingnan, and others were nominated to review them before submitting them to the plenary session for revision and submission to the Shanghai Municipal Party Department for record. The Municipal Party Department Executive Committee and the Mass Training Committee approved the regulations and instructed the federation to file them for future reference. Yesterday, the federation held a standing committee meeting and decided to promulgate the regulations immediately and discussed and finalized the list of preparatory committee members for each district branch to be submitted to the sixth plenary session for approval and announcement. The organizational regulations for the district branches are disclosed as follows: (Organizational Regulations for District Branches of the Shanghai Special Municipality Special District Citizens' Federation) (1) The Shanghai Special Municipality Special District Citizens' Federation may establish district branches for the convenience of association affairs. There is no fixed number of branches. (2) The district branches are directly subordinate to the Special District Citizens' Federation. (3) The organization of a district branch must have the initiation of seven or more qualified citizens and the joint signature of 100 or more people or 50 or more stores, and must be submitted to the Citizens' Federation for approval and forwarded to the Municipal Party Department Mass Training Committee for approval. (4) The name of the district branch shall be "Shanghai Special Municipality Special District Citizens' Federation, [Number] District Branch". (5) The number of executive committee members of a district branch shall be determined according to the number of members and shall be elected by ballot. (6) The term of office for district branch executive committee members is one year. They may be re-elected for consecutive terms. (7) The order of district branches shall be determined by the order in which they are established. (8) These regulations shall be implemented after being approved by the Municipal Party Department.

Local News Two

Former Fudan Queen Zhang Aila

Sues Editor of "Chinese Students"

Listed alongside Huang Baiying... Said to have entered the dance halls.

Zhang Aila believes she has suffered a major insult.

Zhao Jiabi is willing to reconcile... Negotiating out of court.

Miss Zhang Pinlan's alias "Aila," the meaning of which is unknown, acquired the title of "Queen" while studying at Fudan University because of her excellent writing and unparalleled beauty. Later, after Miss Zhang left Fudan and joined the Jianghai Customs Service, the "Chinese Students" magazine, Volume 2, Issue 2, No. 14, published by Liangyou Publishing House on North Sichuan Road, contained an article by Wang Yuanxing entitled "An Analysis of the Incident of Female University Students Entering Dance Halls," which stated that Miss Zhang Aila and Miss Huang Baiying, who recently made headlines throughout the city for being forced to take poison, had entered Shanghai dance halls as dancers, and included Zhang's portrait in the article, placing it alongside Huang Baiying's photo. Zhang believes that the magazine's editor, Zhao Jiabi, intentionally insulted her by publishing this entirely untrue text, which also concerned her personal reputation. Therefore, she hired a lawyer to file a criminal lawsuit against Zhao. Yesterday morning, Judge Cheng Shangfeng of the Special District Court presided over the hearing in the Fifth Tribunal and summoned the defendant Zhao Jiabi, who also hired lawyer Qian Baohe. The plaintiff's lawyer first presented the magazine as evidence and had Zhang Pinlan describe the untruths in the article and the damage to her reputation. She stated that the photo of her published in the magazine was one she had previously lost. Her minimum demand of the defendant was that the magazine publish an apology with the same prominence as the insulting text. In addition, apologies must also be published in the Shen Bao and Xin Bao newspapers in conspicuous places, and the defendant must also formally send a letter expressing his apology. The defendant Zhao Jiabi agreed to most of the plaintiff's demands, but was initially unwilling to publish apologies in the Shen Bao and Xin Bao because the cost was too great and beyond the financial capacity of the defendant's company. However, Judge Cheng advised him not to haggle further and hinder the reconciliation. Zhao then obeyed the court's order, but stated that publishing in the two newspapers could not be forced and must be a certain position. Judge Cheng then adjourned the case to the following Thursday, instructing both parties to negotiate a settlement out of court. If a settlement is not reached by the deadline or if a settlement is reached but then reneged, the case will be summoned for hearing again.

Tragic Incident of Driving with Prostitutes

The Chauffeur is Blameworthy

Yesterday, he was prosecuted in court by the police.

The driving speed exceeded the normal limit.

Prostitutes and their patrons rode in a car to enjoy the moonlit night in the suburbs, and a car accident occurred in Beixinjing. Three prostitutes died, and one or two were injured. The patrons and the chauffeur were also injured. The details of the incident have been reported in this newspaper. The Jing'an Temple police investigated the incident and determined that the disaster was caused by the chauffeur, Wang Chunfu. Although Wang was also injured, he could not escape the blame for negligence. Yesterday morning, when Wang's injuries had slightly decreased, he was brought to the Special District Court and prosecuted under Article 291, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. Judge Wu Tingqi opened the court for interrogation. According to the police lawyer Li Zhishan, the police investigated the scene of the accident and found two sets of tire tracks: one was the track of the wheels when driving, and the other was the track of the wheels when stopping. The two places were 85 feet apart, which showed that the speed of the defendant's car at that time was actually above 35 yards. The Xujing police then reported the investigation process. According to the defendant Wang Chunfu's testimony, he was a chauffeur at the Lanji Auto Company at No. 126 Zhengjia Wood Bridge. That night, the Tiannan Hotel on Changbang Road called to rent a car. At about 11 p.m., I drove car No. 12577 to the front of the hotel. Two men and three women boarded the car and ordered me to drive to Beixinjing for a drive. When passing Chenjia Bridge on Hongqiao Road, my car was traveling east to west when I suddenly saw two cars in front of me traveling east to west at a very high speed. Moreover, the two cars were driving side by side, each with its high beams on, almost as if they were racing. Suddenly, my eyes were dazzled and I could not see clearly. I quickly turned the wheel to avoid them, causing the car to crash into a tree. The five men and women in the car and I were all injured. At that time, my car was not very fast, only about 30 yards, and so on. He also hired a lawyer to defend him and requested permission for Wang Chunfu to be released on bail for medical treatment. Judge Wu ruled that the case involved casualties and that bail should be difficult to approve and ordered the defendant to be held for further interrogation.

Vehicles and other traffic can pass without hindrance.

Lu Genrong's Reply

After the prosecutor appealed the case in which Lu Genrong in the Huang-Lu case was declared innocent, Lu's defense lawyer submitted the following reply:

Criminal Reply (Respondent: Lu Genrong) Defense Lawyer: Song Mingxun Regarding the case in which the respondent was sued for theft, and the plaintiff official disagreed with the judgment made by the Second Retrial of the Jiangsu Higher Court, an appeal was filed. A reply is hereby submitted in accordance with the law, as follows:

Upon review of the original case, the first section of the plaintiff official's appeal stated, "Although a comprehensive review of the entire file cannot prove how the defendant Lu Genrong assisted Huang Huiru at the time of the theft, it is difficult to dismiss his responsibility for transporting the stolen goods," etc. The problem of the innocent verdict of the alleged theft part of the original trial is no longer within the scope of the appeal. As for the point of disagreement, it only concerns whether or not the stolen goods were transported. The appeal arguments are hereby defended. It is necessary to base criminal proof of facts on evidence. If the evidence is insufficient, or there is no conclusive proof of the crime, the defendant should be acquitted based on the suspicion of a crime that cannot be proven. This is the principle of criminal procedure law. In this case, whether the respondent has a suspicion of transporting stolen goods or not, the gist of the Second Retrial of the Final Court was that if the respondent transported the goods stolen by Huang Huiru to the Quxingtai Woodshop after Huang Huiru's theft, he could not be exempted from criminal responsibility, etc. The point to be noted in the instructions is whether the respondent ever deposited the items in the Quxingtai Woodshop. It is now found that this one thing has been clearly and definitely determined by the original trial, and the allegations of the complainant Huang Zhu are false and cannot be believed. Then, the respondent is naturally not responsible for any crime under the criminal law regarding suspicion of transporting stolen goods. According to the plaintiff official's appeal arguments, they are divided into two points: (1) Point A: The only thing the plaintiff official considered relevant here is the extraction of Huang Huiru's statement in the first instance: "The things were taken out on the afternoon of the twelfth. Lu Genrong came out on the twelfth." All the other statements by Huiru in the entire file stating that things were taken out by me on the thirteenth are all ignored. In this regard, the Final Court also recognized it as a suspect in the respondent's crime, but in fact, it is still necessary to seek further confirmation. The judgment in the Second Retrial had already been instructed clearly. Now, the original trial investigation shows that there is absolutely no other confirmed business in the facts, and the second point in the reasoning column of the original verdict has been explained in detail in the case, so it is naturally not allowed to be involved in further inferences. Furthermore, the plaintiff official said, "Huang Huiru's statements have been for the defendant's explanation everywhere," and again cited the car as a proportion. The car's hiring is part of the relationship between harmony and temptation, and is not within the scope of the theft part. I will not list the discussion for now. If it is said whether Huiru's statements are for the respondent to absolve, unless you ask Huiru, it is impossible to prove it. Others are never allowed to freely presume. As for the fact that Huang Zhu beat Huiru on the twelfth, according to Huiru's statement in the file, it is true that Huang Zhu beat her on the twelfth night, but she absolutely denied the phrase "Lu Genrong took it out." Moreover, there is a phrase in her statement, "The things were placed in the downstairs study on the twelfth night." The plaintiff official used Huiru's beating as a presumption to prove that the things had been taken out on the twelfth. How can one have not yet consulted the details of Huang Huiru's statements in the entire file? This statement is inevitably close to conjecture. Secondly, it is based on the statements of the Public Security Bureau. The statements of the Public Security Bureau were not in a question-and-answer format at the time, but were compiled after the fact. Just looking at the four words "carried valuable" in the record, it is definitely not the text that should be in the oral statement. Moreover, the description is based on the phenomena after the case was solved. It is not possible to associate the respondent with suspicion based on this. Moreover, the interrogation of the bureau is not an investigation in the direct trial of the court, and cannot be used as a basis for a decision. The former Dali Temple has a precedent. Therefore, although the intent of the Final Court also recognized this section as a criminal suspicion, it still needs to seek further confirmation in the facts, and it was also explained in detail in the judgment of the Second Retrial. However, the plaintiff official still cited it as proof of transporting stolen goods, which is really out of the realm of reason. This point A cannot be established. (2) Point B: This point is divided into three paragraphs. The first paragraph said that the crime was only a means, and the purpose was to seek wealth. This paragraph traces Huang Huiru's theft to the cause and effect of the crime before adultery. It is impossible to link them together and is not an issue that should be discussed legally in this theft case. There is no value in replying. Second paragraph: This paragraph is the most complex in the plaintiff's argument and is refuted point by point as follows: (Zi) It is said that Huiru and the respondent agreed to escape. The day before, they handed the leather box to Lu to secretly transport out, and they cannot deny that they had no plans, etc. According to this section of the tone, it is no different from the plaintiff official having already determined that Huiru did hand over the things to the respondent and took them away on the twelfth, but it is found that Huang Huiru and the respondent both stated in their statements that the things were taken out by Huiru herself on the thirteenth, and the statements of the two are consistent with each other, which has been described in detail in the first point of the reasoning column of the original verdict, and the plaintiff official completely ignored it and made a judgment. He also attached the words "plans", but he did not know what to base it on. (Chou) It also said that referring to the fact that the things were transported out first on the twelfth and a car was hired to pick up people on the thirteenth, it is undeniable that they were colluding with each other. The car hiring problem is not within the scope of theft and has been explained above. The plaintiff official used this to pull in as collusion in the theft, which seems to be out of the question. (Yin) And said that the defendant stated in the Public Security Bureau that he carried valuable ornaments, etc., not only knew that there were ornaments hidden in the box, but also knew that their value was valuable, etc. The statements narrated by the Public Security Bureau were compiled after the fact and are insufficient to be taken as evidence, as has been explained above. In the end, it is impossible to prove whether the respondent knew that there were valuable ornaments hidden in the box before the Public Security Bureau solved the case. The plaintiff official based his word on this presumption, which is inevitably too ideal. (Mao) It is further said that the defendant served as a teahouse in Huang Zhu's for a long time and knew the family affairs deeply. Huang Zhu was in charge. Suddenly, when they agreed to escape, he handed over the valuable ornaments to him to transport out first, and the details of his escape were obvious. He must not say that he had no foresight. According to this statement, it is even more bizarre. The respondent served as a teahouse and was in charge of external affairs. How did he know how much family wealth Huang Zhu had? The plaintiff official said that the respondent could foresee it when he served as a teahouse. I don't know where he imagined it from.

The third paragraph said that Huiru and the respondent moved back and forth between Suzhou and Shanghai, changing their residences several times, and also pawned the ornaments and ate together. How could they not know the origin of these ornaments? It was found that the things Huiru sold were sold by herself and had nothing to do with the respondent. As for the eating problem after running away, it is not related to theft. The plaintiff official even attributed the eating to the respondent and must know the origin of the ornaments. This statement is not only conjecture, but also inevitably bordering on arbitrariness. Looking at the above points B and C, they first said plans, then said collusion, then said foresight, and finally said how could they not know the origin. It is nothing more than all kinds of speculation. The language in the intention of the Final Court to send the same and retrial to seek other confirmation is just the opposite. This point B cannot be established either. In summary, the ornaments in this case were taken away by Huang Huiru herself on the thirteenth and were not handed over to the respondent for transportation. Huang Huiru has stated this clearly in her statements, and also told him (referring to Lu Genrong) that he only knew that he was wearing ordinary clothes and did not know that there were jewelry, etc. It is credible and unambiguous that the respondent not only suspected of transporting Huang Huiru's theft, but also did not know the facts. The original trial recognized that it was obvious and could not prove the crime, and the judgment of innocence was extremely appropriate. The plaintiff's official's appeal is difficult to say that it is reasonable. Based on the above arguments, I respectfully request the court to review and request to invoke Article 408 of the Criminal Procedure Law to make a judgment rejecting the plaintiff's official's appeal. Respectfully, to the Supreme Court.

The Red Cross Plague Hospital opened yesterday

The Chinese Red Cross Society Tianjin Road Plague Hospital officially opened yesterday. The opening ceremony was held at 3:00 p.m. There were more than 80 people from the military, political, business, and academic circles, as well as the president Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Qian Xinzhi, Wen Lanting, and Wang Peiyuan. Dr. Wang Peiyuan, the president of the hospital, led Chinese and Western guests to visit the various departments of the hospital. The Western guests included Miss Nie Guosi, head nurse of Renji Hospital, Miss Du Tao Baiers, Mr. Sheris, health official of the French Public Works Bureau, Mr. Labai, director of the Health Department, Mr. Tan Chen, president of the Public Concession Fire Brigade, and Mr. Yanalai, dean of the Aurora Medical College. They all praised the hospital's precision and practicality in treating plague instruments. The Western guests criticized the treatment of the plague for being valuable in experience rather than specializing in drugs and equipment. The doctors and nurses of the hospital are all veterans who were the first to treat the plague and hold important positions in medical affairs, so their results in saving lives can occupy an advantage. Later, Wang Xiaolai, a member of the executive committee of the association, generously donated 200 yuan to the hospital's expenses.

Initiation of a Temporary Plague Hospital

The area north of Zhabei Station is vast and densely populated, especially with many civilians. They suffer from epidemics and have no suitable local hospitals. Abolish Bad Funeral Customs in Rural Areas

Joint Proclamation by the Social and Public Security Bureaus

The Municipal Social Bureau and the Public Security Bureau jointly issued a proclamation stating that it has been found that in the rural areas of Gaohang, etc. in this city, whenever a family encounters a funeral, residents nearby, old and young, carry paper money and flock to the funeral home for meals on the occasion of the fifth and seventh days. Even from a distance of four or five miles, they come in groups. Each time, there are as many as three or four hundred seats, and at least eighty or ninety seats. There are many people and mixed voices, and the order is chaotic. The owner is exhausted to cope, and the cook is exhausted to run around. The rich families feel pain in their spirits and bodies, and the poor borrow money and pawn everything, even selling fields and selling property. This kind of bad habit is not commensurate with ability, does not care about people's difficulties, and does not care about people's livelihood, which damages the society more than this. In addition to the Public Security Bureau ordering its subordinates to investigate and ban them at any time, it will also order the municipal commissioners of various rural areas to find ways to guide them to abolish them automatically. In addition, it is specially issued to the citizens of various rural areas, reminding them that material resources are difficult, and funeral etiquette should be called the family's existence or absence. It is natural for neighbors to condole, but they must measure the financial resources of the mourning family. How can they go in groups like beggars? After the proclamation, the citizens of various rural areas should change it if they have it, and encourage them if they don't, in order to frugality and promote thrift. If they still deliberately violate it, they will be severely punished and not pardoned once they are found out. This is specially announced.

Hot Weather

Each Silk Factory Only Works Half-Time

Every year when the hot summer arrives, the silk factories in this city have the practice of temporarily suspending the summer vacation. Recently, the silk market in foreign villages has been sluggish, and the humid heat has invaded people. In the past few days, the temperature in the workshop after noon has often been above 100 degrees Celsius. All the silk reeling female workers are sweating like rain, so they are specially following the example of holding a summer vacation, only working half-time in the morning and stopping work in the afternoon. The full-day work will be resumed after the weather is slightly cooler.
